```


概括该课程章节的TLDR, 以及次章节, 每个章节需要有标题以及TLDR , TLDR需要简练和生动.
注意：在描述步骤时，保持软件界面中的命令名称为原始英文。使用重音符号(`)来标注界面操作路径，例如 `File > Save All`。

```
您是一位专业的视频分析专家，擅长解析教学和技术演示视频。您的任务是仔细观看一段视频，并提取其中的关键信息。具体来说，您需要：

1. 识别视频作者提出的所有实践目标。
2. 对于每个实践目标，详细列出实现该目标所需的所有步骤。
3. 在描述步骤时，保持软件界面中的命令名称为原始英文。
4. 尽可能提取并记录完整的命令路径。
5. 使用重音符号(`)来标注界面操作路径，例如 `File > Save All`。

请以清晰、结构化的方式呈现您的分析结果，确保信息准确且易于理解。您的分析应该能够帮助观众快速掌握视频中的核心内容和操作流程。

我的第一个任务内容:


```

```
I know you can be like a knowledgeable human that can thoroughly understand any text, extract key objectives, and identify Specific tasks. Your job is to review the following text carefully and list all action items for students.

Present the action items for students in markdown format, like this:
### <Key Objectives>
- <list of action items>
...

Note: Use English for all command names and include command paths when possible (e.g., \`File > Save all\`").

List the action items as bullet points with a relevant emoji for each one.

```


```
将视频归纳为若干目标章节以及若干个与该目标章节相关的步骤, 每个步骤需包含"标题 - 详细步骤的解释 - 时间戳" ,  回答使用简体中文.

```

```
将视频分解为若干章节以及若干个与该章节相关的步骤, 例如"""
#### [章节标题]
[该步骤的标题] : [详细步骤的解释]  ([时间戳])
[该步骤的标题] : [详细步骤的解释]  ([时间戳])
""" ,
回答使用简体中文.

editing and mixing it in Audition
and then sending it back

of the course
we'll take a more detailed look at the audio post-production workflow
I'll show you how to edit a single clip in the waveform editor and combine multiple clips together using the multi track editor
We'll learn how to identify and remove various types of noise and repair common recording issues

how to alter and stylize your audio with effects
and how to create a professional sounding mix with some advanced techniques

## 004 Taking a closer look at the Editor panel_原文

In this video
let's take a closer look at the editor panel
since this is where we'll be doing most of our work in Audition
The files that you'll be working with in the Editor panel are first imported into your Files panel in the top left up here
And if you've used Premiere or After Effects before
you might think of this as your project panel
but with one big difference
In the Files panel
you can't actually rename these files or organize them into folders
At the moment I'm looking at what's called the multi-track editor
But if I go over to my Files panel
and I'll just double click one of these files
now I'm actually viewing this in the waveform editor
And I can only work in one of these two modes at a time
I can switch between them using these two buttons up the top here
So if I wanted to jump back to the multi-track editor
I just click here
and now I'm back in that session
Multi track is for working on multiple files and the waveform is for working on individual files
But there is one other big distinction between these two modes
and it's important to understand the difference track is non-destructive
meaning that any changes I make to these clips here can be unmade or adjusted at any stage
So if I go over to this clip here
and I'm just going to turn its volume down just by clicking and dragging
Wellif I decide at any stage
even after I've closed and saved this file
that I want to turn that volume back up
I can just click and drag the volume back up to where it was
It hasn't changed the file on the track
it's only referencing it
Whereas if I was to do the same thing with this file in the waveform editor
so I'll just double click this
and now I've opened it in my waveform editor
The changes that I make here are permanent once I save this file
So if I go over to my volume control here
and I'm just going to turn the volume down
you'll notice that when I let go of this
it's actually gone back to 0 here
And in fact
the whole waveform has been changed
I can
of course
go back to the volume control and just turn this up if I want
but I can no longer see the previous volume adjustment
So at best
I could go up to my edit menu
up the top and undo amplify
and then undo amplify again
But not once I've closed and saved this file
In this mode
we also have this handy spectral frequency dis​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ ## 005 Customizing your workspace_原文

One of the great things about the panel layout in Adobe's Creative Cloud applications is how customizable it is
I have these preset workspaces up the top here that have come with Audition
and I can change to these just by clicking on them here
And there are actually a few that I can't see at the moment
but all I need to do is click this flyout menu here
and I can access all these other workspaces
or I could go up to my window menu
select workspace
and here are all those exact same workspaces
So for example I'm working on a project with video in it
so it would make sense to choose something like edit audio to video
So I just click this and now we have a layout that's better suited to working with projects with video in them
But I can actually customize this further
For example
if I wanted my video panel to be bigger than my multitrack session on the right here
all I need to do is place my cursor in between those two panels and then click
And if I drag to the right I'm making the video bigger and the editor panel smaller
And the same goes for any other panel here
If I go down to my history panel
for example
which is looking a little short
if I click in between here
just click and drag up
now I'm actually making the history panel taller and I'm reducing the size of the panels above it
I might just adjust my video panel as well
There's also a quick way to make any panel temporarily full screen
And to do that
all I have to do is move my cursor over the panel that I want
and I'm going to press the accent graph key
That's the squiggly key below my escape key
And now I'm looking at that editor panel in full screen
Then when I wanted to set this back to the original size it had
I just pressed the accent graph key again
and everything goes back to the way it was
And you can do this with any panel in Audition
So I could go over to my video panel
for example
and if I press Accent Grav
well now I've got a full screen video playback of my session
I'll press Accent Grav to set it back to the way it was
Probably another panel where this would really come in handy is something like your files panel
which has all the files that I have loaded in my multitrack session here
And you can see there's a lot of information in here and it goes left to right as well
So if I wanted to quickly see all of this
just move my mouse over it
accent graph
And now I'm looking at all that information at once rather than having to scroll up and down to navigate it
So I'll just press that key one more time to take it back to the way it was
Now that's if I wanted to change the size of any of my panels
but if I want to change the position of it
that's quite easy as well
So if I wanted to move my video panel down here
all I need to do is go up to the panel
namethis little tab here
and I'll just click and drag down
And you can see I'm getting this purple line that's indicating where the panel is going
And when I let go
it's moved to that new panel location
And I can also do that with any panel
So my files panel
for example
if I wanted to move that up
I just click and drag
And now I've moved it up to the top of my screen
There is another variation on that as well
And that is if I wanted the panel to float on top of all the other panels
So for example
with my video panel here
if I hold down the command key or control
if you're on a PC I'll just click and drag video and you'll see now it's become a floating panel that I can put over the top of anything and I can resize this as well
I can make this nice and big and move it around
I'm not a huge fan of floating panels to be honest
so I'm just going to click the name and drag it back down to the bottom here and it just snaps back into my panel group If you've created your own panel layout and it's something that you want to regularly use
you can actually save that
All you need to do is go up to your window menu and choose Workspace and down the bottom here we have save as new workspace
so I'm going to call this Paul's workspace and I'll click OK
and now the next time I go back to that window menu here
I can actually just choose it from that selection there
but also you'll notice that it's actually added it to these buttons up the top here
So I can very quickly just switch back to it by clicking it up here and even though I've saved this workspace now I can keep making changes to it

you'll become more clear on how you like your panels to be laid out


## 006 Who should watch this fast track chapter__原文

This Adobe Audition Essential Training course is meant for people with varying skill levels
Some have come from other digital audio workstations
such as Pro Tools or Logic Pro
while others have come from video post-production software such as Premiere Pro or After Effects
This fast track chapter is intended for people in those last two categories
so if you are a beginner
I recommend you skip this chapter to avoid getting information overload
If you are a beginner and you'd still like to watch this chapter
just remember that the chapters after this will be more in depth and much easier to follow for those of you who want to dive right into the fast track and quickly learn the basics
here's the project we'll be working on in this chapter

And now all these highlighted clips have been selected
And then I go up to the clip menu and I want to choose Match clip loudness

Probably the one you'd be most familiar with is the peak amplitude here
This is kind of like normalizing a clip where we'll find the highest peak in every clip and set it to a specific level
But in this case I'm actually going to choose the first option it Urbs
And this is actually measuring perceived loudness and it's going to have a more consistent result

monostereo

# 02 Importing Media

## 012 Importing audio files_原文

Before we start working with our audio files
we need to open them inside of Audition
There are a few different ways to do this
and it really all comes down to what you prefer
If you go up to the Files panel up the top here and click this little folder icon here
this is our open file icon
It brings up our open file dialog
And here I can navigate to any files that I want to open
I'll just click this one in the middle here and click open
and you'll notice that what it's done is it's added the file to our Files panel and it's also opened it up inside of my editor panel here
It's important to point out that Audition hasn't moved the file or done anything to it
It's simply linking to the original media
On my hard drive
If I go over to my Files panel and right click and choose Reveal in Finder
you'll see that my file is exactly where it originally was
Now
you may notice that there's another icon next to our open file icon
and that is our import file button
And the difference between this is when we open a file
it will load it in our Files panel and open it in our editor when I click import
and this time I'll select the file at the bottom here and click open
It only actually loads it in our Files panel
It hasn't opened it over here in our editor as well
And this comes in handy when you're working in a multitrack session and you just want to input a file without also loading it in the editor window
Outside of these buttons
there are a couple of other methods that you may prefer to use
Of course
you can always use the tried and true classic of dragging and dropping
So if I just select this file here
I can just drag it straight to my Files panel
or I could have even dragged it straight to my editor panel to load it straight in my editor here
The last method I wanted to mention actually involves the Media Browser panel
And if you can't see your media browser
just go up to your window menu
You want to select Media Browser
Here I've got mine turned on
which is why I have this little check here
And there's this panel over here on the left
With this panel
I can navigate my hard drive without having to use the open file dialog
It's a little hard to see things at the moment
so I might just move this bar across here
and I'll go down to my media drive
I'll just move this bar across so I can see what's in that folder
I'll double click my audio and I'll go into my sound effects folder here where I have all my sound effects for my project
Now this is quite a tight view and I could actually expand this across a bit more by clicking and dragging
What I want to see is all of this panel and to do that I'm going to use the accent graph key
It's also known as the tilde key and it's the one that's underneath my escape key
If I click that while hovering my mouse over the panel
I can now see just that panel full screen
And as you can see here is in addition to just seeing the name of the file I'm also seeing a lot of handy information about the file
So the duration of it
it's sample rate
it's channels
I can see I've got I have the audio loaded here in my editor panel

And this is because Premiere has a non-destructive workflow
It never makes changes directly to its media files
whereas this is not always the case for Audition where you can make destructive changes to the original media if you're in the waveform editor
So to enforce Premier's non-destructive workflow
audition creates new copies of just the audio used on your timeline

# 03 Audio Terminology

## 015 Understanding frequency_原文
Before we jump into working with our audio files in Audition
let's go over a few fundamental concepts
Firstwe'll start by talking about frequency
When sound is created
it travels through a medium
usually air
by changes in pressure in the form of waves
And when those waves reach our eardrums
we interpret that as sound
The timing of those waves is what's known as the frequency
Or to take​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ the word literally
how frequently the wave fluctuates
To show you what I mean
let's look at this file here
Nowyou might guess just by looking at the waveform
that this is three identical sounds played in succession
but if I hit the space bar to play
you'll hear that it's actually three distinct tones and each one sounding higher than the previous
Now
if we move the play head back to the start and zoom in on this
you'll see this isn't actually a solid block at all
It's actually made up of waves
And when we talk about the frequency
we're referring to how long it takes for this wave to complete one cycle like this
The way that we measure these waves is with hertz
or cycles per second
So this particular wave has 440 cycles per second
or rather 440 Hz
The more cycles per second
the higher the pitch of the sound
So if I hover my mouse over this navigator up here
when I get this little hand icon
it means I can click and drag and I'll move across to our next tone
And you'll see that the waves are actually closer together here
Or rather
it has more cycles per second
The tone of this frequency is 880 Hz
And if we go to the last tone on our waveform here
you'll see that they're even closer together with a frequency of 1760 Hz
Although we usually measure in kilohertz to anything over 1000 hertz
So in this case
it would be 1．76 kHz
It's generally accepted that the range of human hearing is somewhere between 20 Hz and 20 kHz
Understanding what frequency is and how it works can be very helpful when working in audio because it allows you to target specific frequencies or ranges of frequencies
Later in this course
we'll look at how we can use things like the spectral frequency display to identify specific frequencies in our files
as well as using EQ effects like the graphic equalizer to make that frequency louder or softer
This leads us to another important concept of audio
and that is amplitude
which we'll cover in the next video


## 016 Understanding amplitude_原文

In the previous video
we discuss frequency or the cycles per second of a sound wave
The other important part of measuring a sound is amplitude
or how much the sound wave fluctuates up and down
Files with smaller fluctuations will be softer and bigger fluctuations will be louder
Looking at this file that I have open in the waveform editor
I can tell just visually that I have three sounds here
and each one is louder than the previous
Let's play back to confirm this
So the way that we measure amplitude is in decibels
or Db for short
And that's a small D and an uppercase B
and that's the scale on the vertical axis here at the top
we have 0 dbfs
or decibels full scale

that's as loud as anything can be
And down the bottom here
we have infinity
or basically silence
This is why all amplitude is expressed as a negative number
because you can't actually go above 0
And the scale is married underneath for fluctuations that go below this line here
or what's known as the zero crossing point
So if I look at these three individual tones
I can tell
looking at this grid here
that this first sound here is about -18 decibels
This sound here is about -12 decibels
and this one here is -6
And I can confirm that by looking at my levels meter down here
which has the same scale
starting with 0 and moving back in negative numbers
So that's amplitude
And along with frequency
they're two very important elements of measuring sound


## 017 Understanding sample rate_原文

When we capture audio digitally
we're not actually recording every single moment of the sound
Insteadwe capture snapshots at set intervals
And these are called the sample rate
And we can see these samples
If I scroll my mouse wheel over this tone here until I can sort of really zoom into it
you can see there's our wave
But if we get even closer
we actually have all these little dots here that are making up the wave
Each of these dots indicates one sample
The sample rate is measured in her​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌tz
and we have some standard rates like CDS
which is 4400
100 Hzand video
which is usually 48000 Hz or 48 kHz
The sample rate is especially important for higher frequencies because they have more cycles per second and you need to make sure the speed at which you're sampling these sounds can accurately capture those cycles
The general rule is that your sample rate should be about double the highest frequency you're trying to record
which is why 44．1 kiloher is as low as you'd really want to go
Since human hearing can reach about 20 kHz
If I create a new file by selecting file
new audio file
you'll see there's the option to choose our sample rate here
And we have some options in our drop down list
There's 44
1 48000
Some audio engineers will set their sample rate as high as 96000 kHz for incredible high quality
Of course
the trade off is that the higher your sample rate
the larger those files will be to store all that extra information
Another factor that will affect the quality of your audio is this option down here
bit depth
which we'll discuss in the next video


## 018 Understanding bit depth_原文

In the previous video
we saw that the sample rate determines how regularly a snapshot of the sound is recorded
Following on from that
it's the bit depth that determines the amount of information stored in each of those samples
The more bits
the wider the range of volume we can have within each sample
I'll create a new file again by selecting file
new audio file
And at the bottom here
you can see here are our bit depth options
A low bit depth of 8 b gives us a dynamic rang​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ of 48 decibels
which doesn't allow for much change in the amplitude
The two most common bit depths you'll come across are 16 b
which is often used for CDS and has a dynamic range of 96 decibels or 24 b
which has a range of 144 decibels
The highest option you can choose is 32 b float
which will allow for the most dynamic range in your recordings
192 decibels
As with the sample rate
the higher the bit depth
the larger your files will be
My recommendation with bit depth would be to choose the highest your computer can handle
which will most likely be 32 b float
even if you're delivering at a lower bit depth
you can always down convert to a lower bit depth later for delivery and keep a higher quality version as a master

# 04 Editing Individual Clips with the Waveform Editor
## 019 Understanding the Waveform Editor_原文

This chapter will focus on the waveform editor
which we used to work on individual audio files directly
It's important to note that the work you do in the waveform editor is destructive to your files
So once I save and close this file
any changes I've made will be permanent
If you'd rather work non-destructively or combine multiple files together
then you'll want to look into the multi-track editor
which we'll be covering in an upcoming chapter
I guess the question is then
why would you ever want to work destructively
Wouldn't we always make changes that can be undone later
This would be nice
but there are certain things in Audition that need to be performed destructively
such as converting the sample rate or bit depth
As well as this
if I do a search on the word process here
all of these effects actually need to be applied directly to the file
They can't be applied any other way
But on top of that
sometimes it's just quicker and more straightforward to work directly with the waveform
For example
I have this file here in front of me
And as you can see
just by looking at the waveform
it's a little too much silence here at the start
Nowrather than bringing this into a multitrack session and trimming it
I can actually just select right here on the waveform by clicking and dragging across
And ## 020 Adjusting clip amplitude_原文

Another advantage to working in the waveform editor that I really like is being able to visually adjust amplitude
‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌To do this
we have this floating panel here
which is also known as the HUD or Heads Up display
If I click and drag over any of these controls here
you can see that I can not only turn up the level
but see the change that it's actually having on the waveform while I do this
And next to the dial
I can see how much I'm adjusting the level in decibels
Nowonce I've released my mouse
the level changes back to 0
This is because it only ever shows you the current volume adjustment
It doesn't keep track of every change you make as you go
I'll just click anywhere in here to deselect this
And I can click and drag this as high as I want up to 15 decibels
But if I did actually want to go higher than that
I can actually type in a value here
So I could type in 30 decibels
and now I've turned this up even louder
Of course
you don't want your waveform to look like this
where the peaks are going over 0 decibels on scale here because this is actually clipping my audio and will sound distorted
So to get back to where I was I'm just going to click undo amplify and undo amplify
and this is the flexibility you get within the wave format it
So while you still have the file open
but it's important to note that once I close the file
I can't undo these changes anymore
At the moment I'm making an adjustment to the overall clip
but I can also use the heads up display to adjust a specific section of the clip by making a selection
So for example
this part of the waveform over here is looking a bit loud
So if I click and drag over this
now when I actually adjust my heads up display I'm only adjusting that section of the waveform
So I can make this a little bit softer
Now you might also notice that after I made that selection
the heads up display actually jumped over to where I am
which is the default behavior in Audition
Wherever I make a selection
the heads up display will follow me
But if I click and drag this gray area of the heads up display
I can actually move this wherever I want
And when I do this
you'll notice that this pen here has turned from gray to blue
This means that I've now pinned this panel to this position in the way for me
it's up
But if you want to go back to the way it was
all you need to do is click that pin
It'll go back to gray and it will go back to its default behavior of following around my selections
So that's how you can visually adjust amplitude in the waveform editor
It's always important to remember
as with anything you do in the waveform editor
this is a destructive process and you can't undo it once you've closed your file
So it's a good idea to make a copy of your original media before you make these changes


## 021 Setting clip levels with normalization_原文

When adjusting the overall gain of your files
sometimes you'll want the loudest peeks of your audio to be a specific level
You can do this very easily using a process called normalization
So for example
with digital audio
the loudest anything can go is 0 db up the top
Here in this file
it looks like my loudest peek is this one here
which is falling somewhere between -6 and -3
And I want to make this file as loud as possible
Nowthe quickest way to do this is to go up to my favorites menu
And here we have two options to normalize
Normalize to -0．1 db or normalized to -3 db
I'm going to choose -0．1 since that's just a fraction under 0 db
And as you can see
it's raised the overall gain of my volume here
And if I go over to this peak and zoom into it by pressing the plus key
you'll see that that highest peak there is just touching 0 db
If you wanted to normalize your audio to a level other than what's available in your favorites
you can use the normalized effect by going effects amplitude and compression normalized process
Here we have the option to choose a percentage or a decibel
I think I'll go with a decibel in this case
And let's say we want to make this file no louder than -10 db
I'll click apply
Now it's lowered the overall gain of the file
If I hover my mouse over the decibel scale here and use my scroll wheel
I can actually zoom in on the decibel level
And you can see here is -10
And now that highest peak is touching that point there
If you do this to a lot of files
it doesn't make sense to do them each individually like this
Insteadyou can use the Match loudness panel
which if you can't see it
go to Window Match Loudness
Here it is over on the left and I have some files over in my media folder in these exercise files that need to be normalized
And all I have to do is select one of them
hold down Shift to select all of them
and I can drag these directly into that panel
And now it's also brought them into my Files panel as well
Now this panel is looking a little bit small for me at the moment
so I'm actually going to hover my mouse over it and press the Accent graph key
which is just below your escape key
And I'm going to click this Compute loudness b​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ which I'll go into later when we discuss multitrack editing

this is how you would adjust the gain directly in the file itself


## 022 Editing with the clipboard_原文

It may seem redundant to be talking about copying and pasting

So I have this music track open in my waveform editor

## 023 Undoing, redoing, and using the history_原文

While I'm going through the things you can do to your audio files
it's probably worth taking a moment to quickly go through how to undo and redo things
as well as there's a couple of special ways to do this in Audition
Most people know that you can undo redo commands with the edit menu
but there's also this handy third command that's unique to the waveform editor
and that is the ability to repeat a command
So I'm just going to select some audio on my screen here
I'll make a selection across this bit of speech
and I'll turn this down
let's say 5．5 decibels
Nowif I wanted to do this to another part of this file or another file entirely
I could just make that selection and go up to my edit menu and choose Repeat last command
And if I have to do this a lot of times and I want to move really fast
I would recommend using the keyboard shortcut
which is Command R or Control R on a PC
Now
if you wanted to get more of an overview of the changes you've made to your file
you can go over to the History panel
which mine is over here
If you can't see this
you can go up to your window menu and select history
And unlike repeat last command
this appli​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌es to both the waveform and the multi-track editor
In fact
you're probably familiar with this panel in a lot of other Creative Cloud applications
Here
I can see everything I've done to the file since I've opened it
and up until I close it I've got the most recent changes
or what's known as history states at the bottom here and the oldest at the top
And what's useful about this panel is that if I wanted to go back to my first change
rather than having to repeatedly press undo
I can just go and click the state that I want to revert back to
So in this case
I was happy with the first amplification change
not the second or the third
So I just clicked these state that I want to go back to
And you'll notice that I still have these other steps here in my history panel
They're just grayed out
So if I feel I went back a little too far in history
I can just click one of them to jump forward in time
Now I can redo all of these changes if I want
but if I go and make a change at this stage
now maybe I'll delete this first part here
You'll notice that I've lost that last amplification stage
and now I can't go back to it
Another thing to keep in mind is that the amount of history states that you can store in Audition are unlimited
which is great if you're indecisive like I am
Howeverthe trade off is that if you're working with long files or if you have a long list of changes
your system might start to slow down as it's trying to keep track of everything
So if you do find your system is getting sluggish and you have no need to hold on to these history states
you can actually purge them by going up to the context menu of your history panel and selecting Clear History
And I'll click yes
And you'll notice that my changes are still here in the waveform
They're just not available to me in my history panel anymore
So both this and the repeat command can be very useful tools
one for making the same change repeatedly and the other for keeping track of all your changes and reverting back to earlier versions of your audio file

# 05 Cleaning and Repairing Audio
## 024 Using the spectral frequency display_原文

Most people are probably used to working with sound using the waveform graph
but there is another way to view our audio files
and that is the spectral frequency display
Whereas the waveform will only show you amplitude
the spectral frequency display letsie and amplitude at the same time
This can be really handy for identifying the frequency of a specific sound or visualizing background noise in your audio file
So I have this file open
and all I can tell is how loud it is
But if I click this show Spectral frequency display button up the top here
now I can see the frequency of the sound as well
rather than having amplitude on the y axis
I now have frequency measured in hertz
Brighter colours are indicating the louder frequencies in my file
So just by looking at this dark area up here
I can see there's no frequencies up there at all
It's basically silent
I can also see that the loudest frequencies are happening down the bottom here
in fact
most of my loudest frequencies are happening below 1 kilo hurts
but you can also have the best of both worlds
If I go up to this divider up the top here
I can just click and drag down
and now I have both my waveform and my spectral frequency at the same time
This is an incredibly useful feature of the waveform editor
especially when you're working with noise reduction and EQ effects
For example
this file has a ringing phone in it
and I can easily see that with these areas here in my spectral frequency display
Let's have a listen just to confirm that
and you get that emotional bond with people
and you really see this stuff firsthand
So not only can I see where the phone is ringing
I can also see the frequency range of the ringing phone
You might also notice if I go back to just the waveform here
I only have one tool that I can select from
and that's the time selection tool
Whereas if I switch over to the spectral frequency display
I now have access to all these other tools here
And that's because I can use them to select specific frequencies
And if you've used Photoshop before
you're probably familiar with some of these
I'm just going to drag the divider back up
So we're just looking at the spectral frequency here
The first tool we have is our marquee selection
and this would actually be really handy in a situation like this
I'm just going to zoom in on this part of the ringing phone here
If I wanted to make a selection of this ringtone here
I could just select the marquee selection
click and drag across this
And now I've selected just that frequency of the phone ringing
And with the loop button turned on
I can just loop through and confirm that this is the phone ringing
Of course
we're just hearing one frequency of the phone
There are actually a few other frequencies up here that would be good to select as well
We can also use the Lasso selection tool
which is for selecting areas other than rectangles
It's probably not quite what we need in the case of the phone here
What I think will help us the most here is this paintbrush selection tool
I'll just click this and as you can see

‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ly been looking at removing noises from our audio in this chapter
but another common area to fix is clipped audio
Audio clipping usually happens when your recording levels were set too high
and you can visually identify clipped audio by these flat waveforms across the top here
This will create distortion or static in your file
As you can hear in this interview
hiring military veterans is a great business decision
The way to fix this in Audition is to use the D Clipper
and I can get to this by selecting Effects Diagnostics de Clipper process
The D Clipper effect is a little different from other effects in that it doesn't open up an effect window as you'd expect
It actually takes me over to this panel called Diagnostics
and it's this panel I'll use to analyse my audio and then repair it
We have some presets that we can choose from here
I think I'm going to stick with the default and then I'm going to click scan to find out how many clipped peaks it can find in my file
Okayso I can see that it's found 167 problems in my file
And if I unclick this settings button here
it'll actually show me a list of all of those clipped peaks that it's found
And if I click any of these
it will actually take me to that problem peak in the file if you find that it's not picking up all of your clipped peaks
you might want to jump into your settings and go to the tolerance
At the moment
mine is set to 1%
and this determines how much variation can be within the amplitude of the clipped audio
But if you do set this too high
it'll start to pick up your healthy peaks as well
So try to keep this number as low as possible
We also have the gain setting up the top here
And this is mainly for files which don't have the headroom to build peaks because they're already dangerously close to 0 db
which is as loud as you can go
In our case
I think we should be fine
we've got a good buffer of about 6 decibels here where we can build peaks
But if not
you would set this to how much you want to turn down the overall audio before audition tries to add the new peaks
Another option that you may want to consider is down the bottom here
and that is the interpolation
This determines how those peaks will be rebuilt
The default is cubic
which is good in most situations and fast to process
But if you have heavy clipping or a short file
I would recommend switching to the FFT setting and using a high FFT size
And then once you're happy with these settings I'll just close this
go back to our list and I'm going to click Repair all for audition to build all of these peaks
And there you are
You can see that audition has fixed a lot of those flat tops in our peaks and have been replaced with more normal looking waves
And I can actually jump between those two states
You can see there's the flat tops and that's what we've replaced it with and let's play back the file to see that everything is sounding better
Hiring military veterans is a great business decision
Okaythat's a big improvement on that file
So that's the D Clipper effect for those cases where you're working with a file that was recorded too loud or too hot
as we say
and you need to repair those clipped peaks in the file

# 06 Combining Clips with the Multitrack Editor

## 029 Understanding the multitrack editor_原文

So far
we've focused on editing individual audio files directly using the waveform editor
And while this is an important aspect of Audition
reallyI do most of my work using the multi-track editor
In this mode
I can cut audio files to tracks
mix them together
cut them up
move them around
and tweak their effects
or without making any permanent changes to the files themselves
The first time you look at the multi-track editor
it can be pretty overwhelming with all the buttons and controls
but it's not so confusing once you get to know it
FirstlyI should say
although it may seem like there are a lot of controls on screen

although now that I've got mute and solo on at the same time I'm not listening to anything at all

although actually they're only one control

our output is set to the master track
but we'll go into some other options later when we discuss mixing with buses and sends
And you'll notice at the very bottom of our track here
we have the master track
And this is where all the other tracks in our session are ultimately being routed to
You can't add clips to this track
And as you'll notice

except it doesn't have the record or monitor input
And that's because you can't record directly to this track either
So if I wanted to turn the volume up for all of these tracks
rather than setting all of these levels individually
I could just go to the master and say I wanted to turn everything else up 12 decibels
And now all of these tracks have been turned up 12 decibels by adjusting the master track
So this is really just a quick overview of the multi-track editor to help familiarize yourself with the interface and make it less overwhelming the next time you open a multi-track set


## 030 Creating a multitrack session_原文

To create a new multitrack session in Audition is very simple
I'm just going to go over to my Files panel here
and I'll select this new file button
click it open
and I'll choose new multitrack session
and you'll be prompted to fill in some details about your session
We have the session name
which is actually the name of the file that will be stored on your computer
And the folder location is where this file will be saved
along with any other files generated by auditions such as auto saves
I'm going to set this to my media folder in this chapter's exercise files
It's important to point out that the audio files you use in your multitrack session don't necessarily have to be saved to this folder
so long as Audition is able to find them on your computer
Beyond that
you can choose from auditions templates
We have some built in templates for different types of sessions here
or you can go ahead and add your own settings for the sample rate
Remember we said that 48000 Hz is what you would use for a video project
4401 hundred is for a I'm going to go with 48000 for our project for the bit depth
unless you have a very old computer I'd recommend going with 32 b float
We do have some smaller options here
but even if you're ultimately delivering at a lower bit depth
you have the flexibility to lower the bit depth on export
but you can't actually increase it
And the master channels down here refers to how many output channels your file will ultimately have
So will it have one channel which is mono
or will it have stereo
which is two channels
or 5．1
which is actually 6 channels
I'll choose stereo in this case
And this all looks fine to me
so I'll click OK
And here is my new multi track session
It has six tracks
although I can't see them all at the moment
I'm actually just going to hover my mouse over these track headers and adjust my scroll wheels so that I actually minimize all these tracks so that they're smaller
So you can see we have track 1 through to track 6
and we have a master track at the bottom here
And adding audio files to this session is very easy
I'm just going to go over to my media browser
navigate to my exercise files where I have a media folder
and I'll just open up the interviews folder and drag some of these into my Files panel just by dragging them over
And I'll drag this clip onto one of these tracks
Any of these tracks will do
And when I let go
it actually commits to that track
If I wanted to add more than one file at a time
I could do that
I could hold down Shift in the Files panel and select multiple files at the same time
And then I'll drag this over to my multitrack session
And what you'll actually notice is that it's actually laying them in one after the other
If I let go of my mouse here
I get this warning message that's saying this is the first time I've added multiple clips to a multitrack session
And what is the default behavior that I want Audition to do in this case
Do I want to add all of these selected files to the same track
or do I want to put each file on its own track
And this is the point where you really have to sort of think about what kind of work you're going to be doing going forward and what is the default behavior that would work best in that case
I'm going to go with all selected tracks to the same track and click OK
But the good thing is is if I want to add these later on
and I actually want one file per track
I can actually hold down the option key and it will actually do the inverse behavior now
So holding down the option key or Alt on a PC will actually I'll copy each file to its own track
And if that's not good enough for you can't even go to your preferences
I'm going to go up to Adobe Audition preferences
If you're on a PC
you'll want to go edit preferences
and if you go down to multi track clips
you can see there's that same behavior here when inserting multiple clips
And you could actually switch that over to a different behavior
I'm going to keep it this way for now and click OK
As you saw
I had six tracks
but when I added these extra two here
it's added another two tracks to my multi track session
But if I wanted to do this manually
I could go up to the multi track menu
select track

Each clip in the multi-track editor has its own built in controls to quickly add fades to the start and end of a clip

it's actually really easy

If I click this and drag it to the right I'm actually controlling the length of my fade in
so if I pull it over here
it's quite a long fade
but I actually want this to start just where that first drumbeat comes in
You'll also notice that I've got this orange line here
This is actually controlling the speed of the fade and at the moment it's a very linear fade that's going on
But if I click the fade icon here and drag down
this has actually now become a logarithmic fade
And that means it's starting quite slowly
If I drag it up now
it's actually starting quite fast
So you can actually have some different effects with your fades here

## 033 Matching loudness between clips_原文

When you combine multiple audio files together in a multitrack session
one of the first hurdles is getting them to sound like they were all recorded at the same level
And with this session here
I have a sequence of different interviews with people speaking at different levels
recorded at different levels
So it's no surprise that I'm going to have to do some work to make it sound like they all have the same loudness
Nowwhen it comes to mixing audio levels
I like to think of it as two different stages
The first is adjusting the clip gain
which is the overall level of the clip
And the next is adjusting the volume
which I reserve more for fine tuning
And although you can get by adjusting just one of these
there is a benefit to doing the gain first
which In the previous video

which is good for making overall adjustments to a clip

you have more control using the clips volume

this is actually the pan control

## 035 Adjusting track levels_原文

In addition to being able to adjust the volume of each individual clip in the multi track editor
you also have the ability to adjust the volume of the track
This means if you keep your tracks organized
as I do
and you put all the same content on the same track
you can now change the volume of all those clips with one control rather than one control for each clip
For example
I have my music track down here
and I've got a bunch of different clips on here
It's all the same music
but the problem is is that my music is actually overwhelming my interviews
I can't hear my interviews at the moment
so rather than going in and setting the levels for each of these individual clips
I can just use the volume control here
And the important thing is to not confuse it with this control here
which is actually a pan control
Now
the way that I'm going to set the volume for this track is I'm actually going to play down the track and adjust this knob so I can find the right mix for my dialogue and the music sitting just underneath it
So I'm going to move to the start of my sequence and I'll press play and adjust this knob at the same time
So in the United States right now
there's a little over 37000 not for profit organizations dedicated to military causes
Okayso that sounds like the right level
And the great thing is is that that level there has been applied to all these other clips down the end here
but this isn't quite what I want
What I'd actually like is for the music to be louder during this start section here where there's no dialogue
And then when the dialogue comes in
I want it to dip down so it sounds like what I actually need to do is keyframe the volume
but rather than doing it to the clip
which would require me to do it to all of these clips I'm actually going to keyframe the track volume
And the benefit of this is that by separating my clips from the keyframes I'll be able to move clips around or add a new music track entirely
but those keyframes will stay where they are
So before I get started
I like to have a visual cue for where I want my keyframes to occur
So I'm just going to move my playhead over to this first interview
and I'll zoom into it and just find the spot where the interview starts
So just about there
So I know that I want my keyframes to happen around this point here
Now I've got my music track already expanded
If you don't
it might look like this
Make sure that you've got this nice and big like this
And in order to get to the track keyframes I'm going to go to this section here where it says read
And next to this is this little arrow
I'll just click this to drop it down and you can see I have this yellow line down here
This is actually the volume keyframes for all of my track
If you're not seeing this
you want to go up to your show envelopes
drop down and make sure you have volume checked
Now the way we add keyframes to our volume envelope here is basically the same way that we add keyframes to our clips
I'm just going to move my mouse over here And when I get that plus symbol next to my cursor I'm just going to click and for my second keyframe I'm feeling a little crazy
I might do things a little bit different
I'm actually just going to drag my play head forward to the place that I want the keyframe to occur and rather than clicking my keyframe there because my playhead is at that point I'm actually just going to click this little diamond here
add keyframe
and it's going to add a keyframe under that play head
Now of course
there's no volume change here at the moment because these two keyframes are at the same level
So what I want to do is turn this keyframe up
but I don't want it to move left or right
So I'm actually going to hold down the Shift key to constrain its direction
And I'll click and drag up
And maybe something like -6 decibels is about right for this
And let's have a listen to that

take note of the volume control for the track over here

there's a little over there

and they're all over here

We also have the ability to clear all keyframes
And please pray that y​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ never accidentally clicked this
Or if you do that
you've got an undo to go back to
We also have these arrow keys here
we can actually jump between our keyframes
And if I have my playhead parked over a keyframe and I click this little diamond

So I could just drag another music track in here and it will have that same volume adjustment throughout the session
So that's how we adjust the audio of the entire track in Audition
whether it's just setting a single increase for all clips on the track or making adjustments over time

# 07 Additional Multitrack Features
## 036 Using clip and track colors_原文

A handy way to keep organised in a multi track session is by using colours for specific clips and tracks
At the moment my clips are all the same color and this makes it difficult to quickly understand what's going on in the session just by looking at it
So what I'm going to do is go over to my dialog track
and at the very start of the header here
I have this colored box
I'm just going to click this
And here I can actually choose a color for the track
Let's choose this pink color here and click OK
And you'll notice that not only has it colored the header of my track
it's also colored all of the clips on the track as well
And what I'm going to do is zoom in on these clips at the start here
And you'll notice if I select this clip and drag it down to the next track
it actually inherits the color of that track
Nowif I click it and drag it back up
it goes back to the previous color
So the color of the clip is dependent on the color of the track it's on
But if I wanted my clip to have its own color
for example
if I just zoom out a bit
hereI have all these clips that are from the same interview subject
And it would be good if I could visually identify that all of these clips are part of the same interview
I'm just going to click and drag across them
S​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ now that I've selected all these clips
and then I'm going to go over to my Properties panel
If you can't see your Properties panel
just go up to your window menu and you want to check properties here
The panel is over here
and I've just opened up my basic settings just by clicking next to it

And you can see this has gone back to inheriting the color of the track that it's on
So this behavior is good to keep in mind
especially when you have many tracks of clips and you need to easily identify specific content
It's also incredibly handy in a collaborative environment because if you're all using the same color scheme
it means someone can jump into your session and easily figure out where everything is


## 037 Grouping clips_原文

When you have a lot of clips in your session
it can be a challenge keeping things in sync as well as having to repeatedly adjust clips that need the same settings
And this is where creating groups of clips can really help speed things up
So for example
if I go to my dialog track here and I expand this out
you'll notice that here I have four clips of Joe's speaking
And every time I want to move these around
I have to select them together so I can move them in sync together
Or if I wanted to adjust the clip gain of all of these at once
againI need to select them every time I want to make a change to that
Insteadwhat I can do is just select them once
And I'm going to go up to the clip menu and go to groups
And here I'll select group clips
And you'll notice that audition has automatically assigned a color to that group so I can visually identify it
Now there's also this icon down here
which is some clips with a circle around it that's letting me know that these are now part of a group
And now rather than having to lasso around these every single time I want to select them
I just click one of them and I've selected all of these clips at once
EssentiallyI can now manipulate these separate clips as if they're one clip
Now I can move them all together
Or if I wanted to adjust the gain
I can just select one of them
go over to my Properti​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ panel where I have my clip gain
and I'll turn this up
And you'll notice that not just this clip has turned up its gain
If I zoom in here
all of them have had their gain turn up by the same number
Nowthere will come a time where I will want to adjust the gain of just one of these clips separately
And rather than having to go and ungroup these and then group them again
there is an easier way of doing this
and that is by going up to the clip menu

And there's a very handy shortcut here
So I don't have to go to the menu every time
Once I do that
if I deselect these clips and then click on one of them
now I'm only selecting just that clip
So I can go in and make a change to that and it won't affect the entire group
I haven't ungrouped the clips
I've just disabled the grouping and I can easily enable that again by just going back to my menu or using the shortcut if you prefer to do that and uncheck suspend groups
Now when I select this I'm back to selecting all of them
but as well as that

and you'll notice that all those clips have also returned to their original color

I also really recommend using this feature with something like the essential sound panel
which we discuss in the next chapter to make it easier to keep track of the changes that you're making


## 038 Adding markers_原文

To keep organised
sometimes you may want to mark specific sections in your multitrack session that you'll use regularly
or to keep track of feedback from producers
And for this
you can easily add a marker by going over to your marker's panel
I can't actually see mine at the moment
but if I click this little flyout menu here
I can see there's my markers panel there
If you're not seeing it
just go up to your window and make sure you have markers checked
And over here we have this little button here
add marker
so I can just move my playhead to a particular point in my session and I'll just click the button and now it's added a marker to my session that I can always come back to
Now there is an even easier way of adding a marker to your session
and I'll just move my playhead over here

## 040 Re-editing music with Remix_原文

In my own work
I do a lot of editing of music tracks
and it's very rare that the music track I'm using for a project is the exact length I need it to be
So I'll usually need to cut out repeated sections of the music to make it fit
Now you can either do that manually
which does take time
or you can use a magical feature in Audition known as Remix
With Remix
Audition will analyze your track
determine where there are repeating sections in your music
and re-edit the track so that it fits And let's go through some of these settings here
First
we have the edit length
and this is where we can tell Remix to cut the song using shorter segments or longer
And at the moment you can see it's actually set to long segments
which is why we only have one edit over here in our music
But if I slide this over towards 50
we're actually going to allow audition to actually have shorter segments in the music
And you can see now it's placed two edits in our music track
Let's have a listen to that to see what kind of a change it's made to the music
Okay
that actually sounds a little bit more interesting to me
Beyond the edit length
there are some other things that we can play around with here
We have the features setting
which tells Remix what is more important when it edits the music
the rhythmic elements or the timbre elements of the song or the harmonic elements of the song
Think of this as the difference between dance music
which has a consistent beat
or classical music
which has a complex melody
Below that
we have the minimum loop where we can tell remix what is the shorter segment of music in beats
I think the best thing to do is to just play around with all these sliders and see what different edits you can create

And this refers to how much over the target duration audition can go

50 seconds and 20 frames
This is how much we were asking audition to shorten this clip down to
But if you look at our actual remix duration
