so about 2 seconds longer than what we were asking from Audition
And if I actually move across the clip over to the end here
you can see we're actually overshooting that marker that we originally snapped to
And the reason for this is because music is based on tempo
meaning that it can't perfectly hit certain durations
But if we did want this to be a precise length
we can actually go over to the Properties panel and check this box here
stretch to exact duration
And what this is going to do now is actually speed up or slow down our clip in order to make sure that it hits that perfect duration
And you can see that over here on our timeline now
So this clip has actually been sped up
And if I play this back
you can actually hear the result
And that tempo change isn't so noticeable that it's a problem
So I'm happy to go with that
I can
of course
refine the stretch settings that Remix has applied by going up to my stretch settings up the top here
as we discussed in the previous video
So that's remix
a very remarkable tool I've got to say
And I've seen it work with all different types of music
from dance to classical
The one hurdle you will hit with remix is when you use music with lyrics
because although remix is really good at re-editing music
as you can imagine
it can't just put the first half of one verse next to the last half of another verse and expect it to make sense
But otherwise
it's an amazing tool and it has literally saved me hours in the edit suite


## 041 Creating computer-generated speech_原文

More often than not I'm editing a project well before a professional voiceover or narration is recorded
and so I'll need a temp voiceover to help me time out my edits
And for this
I often use the Generate speech function in Audition
Now it certainly won't replace professional voiceover artists
It's still going to sound artificial and slightly robotic
but it will save me having to record and re-record a voiceover while I settle on the script
To do this I'm just going to make sure that I have the playhead parked at the point where I want to add the narration
and I'll also make sure that I select the track that I want to send the narration to
And then I'll go up to the menu
up the top​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ Before we start recording in Audition

‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ment to check the hardware settings in our preferences
Now I'm on a Mac
so I can get to my preferences by going up to the Adobe Audition menu here
going to Preferences
If you're on a PC
you'll need to go to Edit Preferences
and we want to choose the audio hardware options here
Although on both platforms
the preferences should look the same except for a few small differences
It's also worth mentioning that your sound card is most likely different to mine
so not all the settings will be exactly the same as what you see on screen here
Up the top under Device class
I have Core Audio
which is what the Mac operating system uses to handle audio for applications
And that's actually my only option to choose from here
If you're on a PC
you might have different options here like Mme Asio or Wa s API
which are all different ways Windows talks to your sound devices
Either Asio or Wais API are good choices
Againthis is all dependent on what sound card you're working with
Underneath device class
we have our default input and output
So what device we're using to record and listen to audio
Then down here we have the IO buffer size
Although if you're on PC
this is actually called latency
Latency is the slight delay you might hear when recording and listening to audio at the same time
Basicallythis setting controls how hard your sound card is working
To reduce this delay
by default
it's set to 512 samples
but really
there's no single number that works across all systems
What you should aim for is the lowest number that you can set this to without your audio dropping out or popping and clicking
That's the sound of your sound card struggling to keep up with the level of latency
It might take some trial and error to find the right setting for your specific hardware
Underneath that
we have the sample rate
and it's important to set your hardware to the same sample rate as the audio file you're working on to avoid your hardware having to resample your audio on the fly
which may make things sound odd
Although rather than having to go to your preferences and change this setting every single time
what you could do is check this box here
attempt to force hardware to document sample rate
and basically this will set the sample rate to whatever file you're working with at that time
It may create a slight delay at first as the hardware switches sample rates
but it will help you avoid any weird sounding audio from your hardware resampling
As you can probably tell
a lot of the settings here are very dependent on what kind of sound card you have installed
And in fact
I can get direct access to my sound card by clicking my settings
But and here
but this video should give you a basic idea of where to go to configure Audition before you begin recording

In addition
you have the choice of recording in either of the editor modes
If all you wanted to do was to record to a single file
then you'd choose the waveform editor
But if you wanted to record audio from a multitrack session and then mix it with other files I'd recommend doing this in the multi-track editor
In this video
we'll focus on the waveform editor
and then we'll cover the multi-track editor in the next video
Before I start recording
I need a file to record too
so I'll go up to my Files panel and I'll select the new file button and choose new audio file
I'll name this voiceover and I'll keep the sample rate at 48000 Hz because we'll use this in our video
I'll keep the channels as mono because I'm only recording with one microphone
and I'll keep the bit depth at 32 b float and click OK
Before you begin recording
it's good practice to test the level of your microphone
and you can actually do that with the levels meter down here
I'm just going to right click this panel and select meter input signal
And now I'm getting feedback on how loud or soft my recording will be
And I want it to be a strong
clear signal
but I don't want it to be so loud that it goes over 0 decibels and starts clipping
If you see this box here start to light up red
that means that your audio has been clipped and may sound distorted
And that's what we want to avoid
So I'm pretty happy with this
I'm going to go over to the record button
Now you'll notice there's also the shortcut key shift space
but I'm just going to click this to start recording and then I'll record my voiceover to find out more
visit project railo dot com dot
and then I'll go over to the stop button to stop our recording
and there's our recorded voice-over file
I'll just click anywhere to deselect this
Now it's really important if I wanted to continue recording to this file
not to leave my playhead here
because if I press record at this point
it will actually start to override all of this that I've already recorded here
So what I should do if I want to continue recording is to just drag my play head to the end
and then it will actually record beyond that point
Another really important thing to keep in mind at this stage is that our file is over here in the files panel
but it has this little asterisks next to it
And that's telling me that this file has not yet been saved
So it's not being saved anywhere on my computer
And if I was to close audition and not save this I'd actually end up losing that file
So it's always good practice after you've made a recording to save it first

I can trim this clip just like any other to get rid of some of that stuff at the end there
Now
when we did this in the waveform editor
it didn't actually save the file until we went up to the file menu and chose save
It's a little bit different in the multi-track editor
It actually automatically saves the file for us
And I can tell that if I select my clip here and I'll right click it
And what I want to do is reveal the clip in the Files panel
you'll see there's no asterisks next to the file here
So the question then is
if this is saved
where has it saved it
Because I certainly haven't sent a location for it to save this file
And we can find that out just by right clicking the file here and saying reveal in Finder
And what I'll see is it's actually created this recorded folder next to my session that it's automatically putting my recordings into
rather than me having to manually record it as I did in the waveform editor
So those are some of the differences between recording in the waveform and multi-track editors
I think a good rule of thumb is if you need to record a file on its own
go to the waveform editor
But if it's something you need to edit and mix with other files
and the multi-track editor is the way to go

# 09 The Essential Sound Panel
## 045 Using the Essential Sound panel_原文

Before we dive into working with effects in Audition
first I want to show you a panel that's dedicated to commonly used effects in audio mixing called the Essential Sound panel
If you can't see this panel over here on the right
you can quickly get to it by going up to your window menu and selecting Essential Sound
Although you can also get to it the way that I did by going to my Workspace flyout menu here and selecting essential video mixing
And this is a layout that's good for working with video files and long sessions and the essential sound panel at the same time
So if you've ever used the lumetri panel for color work in Premiere Pro before
it's a very similar approach
The idea behind it is to simplify the audio mixing process and make it more intuitive for people who are not sound engineers
So let's take a look at how this works
The first thing to note is that this panel is only available to me if I'm in the multitrack session
if I was to select one of these clips and double click it
you'll notice that the panel is now grayed out and we can't use it
So I'll go back and select multi track to make sure I'm in this view here
The methodology behind essential sound is pretty simple
All I need to do is select a clip or multiple clips at the same time
and then I go over here and assign a mix type
So these four items here are the most common elements of a mix
The dialogue
the music
the sound effects
and the ambience or background sound
Since we've selected a clip on our dialog track here I'm going to select dialog as our mix type and now based on that assignment I'm presented with a range of settings that are specific to working with dialogue
Not only that
but the order of everything is designed to lead you through the mixing process
So logically
the first thing you would do when you're working on some dialogue is try and unify the loudness
followed by repairing any sound issues with it
and then you'd move on to improving the clarity of that sound
I can check and uncheck these boxes here
and I can turn on particular effects that I want
and I can adjust the settings of these effects just with these sliders here just by dragging them up or down
It's a much simpler interface that makes working with these effects much easier than having to understand the intricacies and nuances of each particular effect
Once you've assigned a mixed type to something
If I was to deselect this
and now I can't remember what I'd assigned as my dialogue here in my session
I can very easily select it again just by going up to my edit menu
going down to select
and all the way down the bottom here
I have clips of mixed type
If I select dialog
it's going to select that clip again
But the great thing is that the Essential sound panel is not an effect in itself
It's actually adding b​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ which is a common issue in audio

also known as sibilants

Our first setting here is dynamics
And dynamics refers to the peaks in your audio
Do you have someone speaking whose voice starts very loud and then goes very soft and then goes loud again
And what dynamics will do is help level out that dynamic range and reduce the difference between the quieter and louder moments of their speech

and I'm just going to creep this up as I listen to it

the more it should be reducing the difference between those things

and my clip has gone well beyond that

And if you watch the earlier videos on stretching time and working with remix
this is basically both those exact same features
but with some limitations
Stretch will speed up or slow down my clip in order to try and make a new duration
And Remix is actually going to look at my music and cut out any repeated sections to try and make a new duration since we need to reduce this down to 50% of what it was almost
I don't think stretch is really going to help us because it's just going to speed up the music too much
So in this case I'm actually going to select Remix
And right now it's analyzing my music
looking for any repeated sections in there that it can cut out before I've even requested it to make any cuts
And the next step is to go in and add a target duration
So I know that this actually needs to be about 50 seconds and 20 frames
So I'll type this in 50 20
And there you go
it's already cut my music down to 50 seconds
and if I just zoom in on this here
you can see I've got this gray jagged line

So this is much quieter than that

# 10 Working with Effects

## 050 Applying effects in the Waveform Editor_原文

As I've been saying throughout the course
the big difference between working in the waveform and multi-track editors is that the waveform is a destructive process that will permanently change your file
whereas multi-track is a non-destructive process that we can continually tweak even after we've closed the session
And this is certainly the case when applying effects
But there are some different ways to add effects in the waveform editor that can give you a bit more flexibility
GenerallyI prefer to work with most effects in the multi track editor
but there are times where making changes in the waveform editor can be beneficial and in some cases unavoidable
The first and most obvious way to add an effect in the waveform editor is to use the Effects menu
So just go up here and select Effects
And here we have all of the effects that we can choose from
And in fact
if you see any effect that has process at the end of it
these effects can only be applied in the waveform editor
so they'll actually be grayed out in the multi track editor
So as an example I'll select this basic Amplify effect and I'll just turn this up a bit
maybe somewhere around about 12 decibels
And when I'm happy with the level I'll just click apply and you can see that that has updated my waveform
Now of course
if I wanted to step back to the way it was
I could just go up to my edit menu and choose Undo Amplify
But after I close and save the file
any changes I make will be committed
Now there is another way to add effects in the waveform editor
and it will still ultimately make permanent changes to the file
It gives you a bit more flexibility outside of using your undo history
and that's adding effects in the effects rack
If you can't see your effects rack at the moment
you can just go up to your window menu and check Effects Rack
And here's mine over here on the left
And what we have here is 16 slots and I can add an effect to each of these slots and stack them on top of each other to affect our waveform here
So I might just deselect this for now
And I'll go up to slot one in our effects rack
And what I do is just click this little flyout menu here
And if you look at this
this actually looks a lot like the effects menu that we had up the top
the exact same options that we have here
So if I go back
and maybe I'll just add the exact same effect
now I'll add an amplify effect
Actually
it's remembered our settings from before
but you might notice that something's a bit different here
We don't have an apply button anymore
although if I was to play back my waveform
manI did these great things and they just extol the it is actually louder than it was before

Let's have a listen to this
the virtual leadership capability
and now it's also it's gone softer

now it's back on with that
I'm not sure if that's true
so we can actually hear the result of the effect
It's just not updating the waveform here
And if I close this window just by clicking this red X here
but then I decide I actually want to go back and tweak that amplify setting a bit more
All I need to do is double click the effect
it brings up the same dialog box again
It's remembered my setting from before
and I can just set this to something else
Maybe we'll set this to 6 decibels
and now I've updated that effect
I can also add additional effects here
we've got 16 slots to work with
so maybe for the second slot I'll click our flyout and go down to reverb and I'll add a convolution reverb

but if I decided that I actually wanted the reverb to be applied first and then the amplify on top of that
I could just click there and drag it up
And now I've actually swapped the order of these effects
Although if I decided that I didn't need the Amplify effect at all
I could just select it and press delete
and now it's been removed from my stack as well as being able to layer effects like this
I also have these input and output meters down here
which allow me to monitor the input and output signal
So here is the original signal of the effect
And this is after all of these effects have been applied
And if I was to play this back
you can actually see that the original signal of the audio was actually louder and my output signal now after I've applied this convolution revert

or decrease it

So a setting of 0% all the way down here is basically no effects applied at all

## 051 Previewing effects_原文

When you're working with effects in the waveform editor
there's a really useful way to view the resulting waveform before those effects have been applied
Using the preview editor
you can use it regardless of whether you're adding effects with the Effects menu or the Effects rack
although it's with the Effects rack that I find it's the most helpful because there I'll be stacking effects on top of each other and not getting any feedback on how they've changed the waveform until the end when I click apply
So if I go over to my effects rack over here and I'll go and add a simple effect like this amplify effect
and maybe we'll just turn this up to something like 10 decibels
And although I have increased the amplitude of my file
I can hear it by playing bad
Sayhey I'm a great leader
Look
it hasn't actually updated in my waveform here at all
I can't actually see it reflected here
but if I go to this icon in the top right of the waveform editor show preview editor
it now divides my screen into 2
And at the top
I have my original audio
And down the bottom here
I have my preview editor
And this is showing me what the waveform will look like after this effect has been applied

## 052 Effects in the Multitrack Editor_原文

We've just looked at applying effects using the waveform editor
but as I've said before
I usually prefer to work with effects in the multi-track editor wherever possible because it's a non-destructive process
Other than this big difference
the actual method for applying effects is actually the same with a few minor variations
So let's say I wanted to add an effect to this clip here
All I would need to do is select the clip and then go over to my effects rack
I'll make sure I've got clip effects turned on and then in the flyout menu here I'll choose something like let's add an EQ effect
This time let's add the FFT filter and we'll choose the Kill the mic rumble effect here
And we can add up to 16 different effects using this effects rack
Maybe I'll just add another one here
maybe just an Amplitude D Essa
and maybe we'll go with the default for that one
I can also add effects to this clip just by going up to my Effects menu
and he will choose like a reverb
a studio reverb
And you'll notice even though I've added it using the effects menu
it's still added that effect over to my effects rack
And as you can probably tell
this effects rack is really just the same effects rack that we were using in the waveform editor
So what is the difference in this case
Wellfor one thing
I don't have an apply button down the bottom here
I don't need to permanently commit these effects to files before I save and close the session
I can always come back to them and tweak them further after I've closed Audition
The other difference is these two buttons up the top here
we have clip effects and track effects
so at the moment I have clip effects highlighted
which means whatever clip I have selected I'm adding my effects to that
But if I go over here and select track effects
now I'm looking at the effects rack for the entire track
So if I go in here and add something like a reverb
let's add a convolution reverb this time and that all looks good to me
Now this reverb effect is being applied to all of the clips on this track here
and it means I can control these clips with one effect rather than an individual effect for each clip
But still
if I click back to my clip effects
you can see they're still all here as they were before
If you find it difficult to keep track of your clip effects and your track effects
a handy way to get around this is to go over to your multi track session
And I'm just going to expand this track out now so I can see it quite clearly
And you can see here is the effects rack for this track
how I got to this view
Maybe you're looking at something like this at the moment
which is just the input and output controls
To get the effects rack up here
you just need to go up to the top and selec​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ the Effects button

If I clicked track effects here
in fact

like maybe a different type of reverb
like studio reverb
and that will automatically be updated in my track effects over here
When you have a lot of track effects stacked on top of each other
especially CPU intensive ones
and you find that they're blowing your machine down
there is actually a way to speed up playback by going down to the bottom here and clicking this pre render track button
And what this is going to do is temporarily create an audio file of the track to speed up your playback
So if I click it here
you can see it actually calculates the render file
And now when I play this back I'll be playing off a rendered file rather than having the CPU play it in real time
If I go into this effect again and maybe make a tweak to it
maybe we'll choose something like outside club
it will automatically update that render file for me
So that's how we apply effects in the multitrack session
And as I said
this is my preferred way of working with effects inside of audition because I have the flexibility to change things along the way


## 053 Using Compression Effects_原文

Now
let's talk specifically about some of the effects in Audition
For me
compression is 1 I use in almost all of my mixes
And I don't mean compression as in file compression
which is used to reduce the size of a file
Audio compression is an effect used to reduce the louder parts of your audio and make the overall recording more consistent in terms of amplitude
So for example
I have this clip marked in my session here
and I'm just going to zoom into it for a moment
and I'll expand out the track as well so we can see it a bit better
And the problem I have here is this is some dialogue in our video here
And I have some uneven peaks in the dialogue
You can see it's quite loud here and here and here
and quite soft in other parts
And it would be good if I could actually level that out and make it all consistent
Now
compression is something that I usually prefer to apply in the multi-track editor as I am right now because it allows me to continually adjust the settings rather than have to commit to them
But for the purposes of showing you what this effect is doing I'm going to go into the waveform editor where we can better visualize what happens once the effect is applied
So to open this clip in the waveform editor
all I need to do is double click it
And now we've opened it up
And I'll also zoom out so we can see all of the clip just by clicking this button up here
And I'll just move the play ahead to the start and we can have a listen to how this sounds side by side is we're in difficult situations
facing adversity
facing the elements
the environment
and you can
you can bluff your way through a 45 minute interview
okay
So you can hear that his voice is kind of louder in parts and softer in others
And if I wanted to go in and adjust this manually
what I would need to do is zoom into some of these peaks like this loud one here and I would turn this down just like that
And then I'd jump over to the next peak
select it
and turn it down
And that's fine if you've only got a few peaks to work with
but it can be quite time consuming if you've got a very long file
And this
this is where compression comes in handy
I'll just zoom out here
so we can go back to seeing everything
And I'll just undo those changes that we made
So to add compression to this file I'm just going to go up to my effects menu
down to amplitude and compression
And there's a few different compressors to choose from here
I'm going to choose the one at the very bottom
which is the tube modeled compressor because it's very simple and straightforward to work with
And the first thing I'll do is go into my presets and just see if there's a preset that's appropriate for what I'm trying to do here
And we've got this one down here
voice leveler
that sounds about right
So I'll select this
So when I add a compressor to my wave file here
I imagine I've just said to somebody
lookthere's some moments in my audio here that are a little too loud
and I'd like to turn them down
And if I was that person
the first thing I would say to them is
wellwhat do you consider to be too loud
And that's where our first setting the threshold comes in here
That's the point at which we consider a peek in our audio to be too loud
So just looking at my waveform here
I'll just move my effect window out of the way
I can see that a lot of the quieter parts of the speech here are happening round about -18
maybe -15
and that's the stuff that we don't want to be affected by the compressor
So for my threshold I'm going to go in and type -15
So anything above -15 I consider to be too loud in this file
If it's below -15
it's fine
I don't need to touch it
The next question I would ask is
wellhow much do you want me to turn these files down by and that's where the ratio comes into play
And this refers to how much we're going to turn down the peaks that go over the threshold
So say I set this to something like 5 to 1
Wellthat means that for every five decibels
that one of these peaks goes over the threshold
it will be reduced to just 1 dB over the threshold
So this huge peak that's hiding behind my effects window over here
let's just move this out of the way a bit better
I can see that that's actually falling at about -5
that's actually 10 decibels over my threshold
10 decibels more than -15 decibels
so that means that after compression has been applied
this should actually now be two decibels over
So it should be more like -13
Before we move on
let's get an idea of how these settings are affecting our waveform
I'm just going to go up to the top right here and turn on our preview editor so we can see our original audio across the top and down the bottom
we have our new compressed audio and you can really see the difference here
Lookin our original audio up here
we have this high peak
it comes all the way down to here and then comes back up and here the difference is much
muchmuch
much smaller and this is going to make it easier for people to listen to this voice as well
What I really like about this tube modeled compressor is this gain reduction meter that we have here
and when this flash is red
that means the compressor is turning the audio down and we can actually see how much it's turning it down by how much it light
it's up on this meter here
so if we don't see any red here at all
that means that no audio is being affected
So if I play this back now
we should see a very strong red light at the start and then it should disappear around this spot here
side by side is we're in difficult situations facing adversity facing the elements
the environment and you can
you can bluff your way through a 45 minute interview
okayso that's sounding much better
And we've really tamed some of those wilder peaks in our audio if you do find that some of your peaks are still sneaking past the threshold
you may want to play around with the attack and release settings here
attack is how quickly the compressor reacts to a level that's above the threshold and release is how soon the compressor returns to the original level
And these are both measured in milliseconds
And then finally
once we've leveled off those peaks
we can actually use the output gain to turn everything up
So before our highest peak over here was -5
now it's as low as something like about -13 over here
so let's turn everything up 8 decibels to get back to that level
And now this looks much better
That peak is back to where it was before

## 055 Using Reverb Effects_原文

Reverb effects have the magical ability to take a sound and place it in a very specific location
The name reverb is actually short for reverberation
and it refers to when audio bounces off walls and other surfaces in a room
Every room will have its own unique reverb based on how many surfaces there are
the size of the room
and how much those surfaces absorb sound
just to name a few factors involved
Sometimes reverb gets confused with echo
and although they're both somewhat similar
they're really not
The sound of reverb is much more immediate
and we perceive it as being a quality of the original sound
whereas echo happens with more of a delay and sounds like distinct repetitions of the original sound
I often use reverb to give sounds a sense of space and ambience in my mix
This could be something as straightforward as taking a cleanly recorded sound effect and making it sound like it's being recorded in a specific room
or just adding a bit of energy to a voiceover
For this example I'm going to show you a couple of reverb effects using this dialogue from our project relo session
But I must admit I wouldn't normally add reverb for this
It can actually be a bit distracting for interviews
but it should be fine for the purposes of this exercise
I'll go over to the effects rack for our track here and I'll click our little flyout menu and all of our reverb effects are over here
We've got a few to choose from
I'm going to choose the studio reverb
This is probably the simplest and most straightforward reverb effect you can choose
and it's also the least CPU intensive
Let's stick with the default preset that we have here and have a listen to how this sounds veterans out there
if you took each veteran individually and help them get a job
So you can certainly hear that I'm going to toggle the power state on and off so you can hear what the original like and what the effect is like veterans out there if you talk
So it's all veteran individually and help them get it out and now it's on here
Now let's move on to the next one
To the next one
We have thousands of
there are a few settings that we can play around with here
So we have the room size at the moment this is set to 70
but we can turn this up as high as 100
Let's listen to what 100 size room sounds like if you took each veteran individually and help them get a job
Okayhere
now let's move on to the next one
Okay
so now it sounds like he's in a church rather than a small office
We also have the decay time here
so how long it takes the reverb to ring out
and this is measured in milliseconds
Let's turn this up a bit higher as well

# 11 Advanced Mixing with the Multitrack Editor

## 057 Understanding the mixer panel_原文

When you get to the mixing stage of your audio project and you have a lot of tracks like I do
it helps to work in the dedicated Mixer panel
which I can get to just by clicking this Mixer tab next to our Editor tab here
If you're not seeing this
you can also get to this just by clicking window and going to Mixer
And this panel has been designed to look like an actual audio mixer
and it may look a little overwhelming at first
but it's basically the same controls that we had over in our multi track editor
only now they're arranged from left to write rather than top to bottom
As you can see
here are all my tracks with corresponding track names here
So the idea is at this stage
we've finished editing the audio in all our tracks
and we just want to focus on adjusting the levels and how all these tracks are being combined in the mix
That's why we can't actually see any clips in this view because our screen real estate is being used to show more tracks and other controls instead
So of course
if you are working in this view
it's a good idea to have very clear track names so you know exactly what track you're working on
I can actually go in and change any of the track names just by clicking on them and then retyping the name that I want
And this actually gets automatically updated over in your editor panel as well
If I click back
you'll see this is actually now sound effects 0 3
And same thing goes for moving tracks around as well
You can actually move any of these tracks around just by clicking this little patch up the top here
I'll just click and drag and we get the blue line to show us where this track will actually be placed
When I let go
it's been moved here
If I go back to my Mixer panel
it's been moved here as well
Probably one of the first things you'll notice about the Mixer panel is that we have much bigger volume controls down here
and I can actually drag these sliders up and down to adjust the level of the overall track
What I also really like about this control here is I can just click the dial and now I can use the up and down arrow keys to move up 1 dB at a time
If I hold down shift and use the arrow keys I'm actually moving three decibels at a time
Of course
I could also go in and just type the actual level that I wanted here
And I can also reset this just by holding down the option key or alts if you're on a PC and just clicking this dial
that resets us back to 0
Above this I have my panner control
that's if you're working in a stereo session and I can use this to pan the whole track to the left speaker or to the right
If I hold down shift
I can actually pan this a little faster
And much ## 059 Mixing multiple tracks with buses_原文

Earlier
we looked at how you can adjust all the clips on a single track with the tracks controls
But what if you wanted to adjust multiple tracks all at once
Wellthis is where bus tracks can really come in handy
So in the case of our project relo session
here I've organised all of my interview clips so that I have each interview subject on their own track
This means I don't have to add effects to each individual clip
I can just adjust them to the whole track
But now I want to be able to adjust all these interviews at once
So how can I have the best of both worlds if I go over to my track header here
and I'm just going to scroll my mouse wheel to expand each of these tracks
you'll see that we have our output setting here
And at the moment
it's set to the master track
which is the final mix down for all these tracks
To assign a different output
all I need to do is select our list
I'll go over to bus and I'll add a new stereo bus track
And here it is
my new bus track
It's actually named it Bus A
but I think I'll call it something a little bit more meaningful
like dialog bus
And this track is unique from my other standard tracks in that I can adjust its volume
I can pan it
I can add effects to it
The one thing I can't do is add clips to this track
I can only route other tracks to it
So right now I have my dialog track for Mike here
and that's being routed to my dialogue bus
and my dialogue bus is being routed to my master
So now let's go ahead and route all of our other dialog tracks here
So I'll just go to my master and I don't need to add it anymore
I can just select it from this list here
And I'll do the same for all of my dialogue tracks
And this is going to give me control over all of them in terms of effects and volume
And I'll just do this one as well
So now let me just zoom out again
So we don't need to see all of these
Now I have a lot of control here
I'm actually just solo all of these dialog tracks just by clicking the solo button on my bus now
But if I expand this out as well
I can also control the volume of all of these dialog tracks as well
Just by using the volume here
you can see that if I play this track back over 37000 not for profit it down dedicated to military causes
But of course
I can also adjust the volume of each of these individual tracks as well
And then with the dialog bus on top of that
I might just set this back to 0 by holding down the option key and clicking it
And as I said before
I can also control the effects for all of these tracks with the effects on my bus tracks

## 060 Mixing effects with sends_原文

Previously
we talked about bus tracks
which allow us to route multiple tracks to one track and make adjustments to all those tracks at once
With send tracks
it's kind of the inverse of that idea
Send tracks allow us to take one track and route it to one or more other tracks so that we can adjust each instance of the track separately
Nowthis is definitely something that you'd reserve for more complex mixes
and you probably won't use them as commonly as you would simply routing to bus tracks
but they can be very handy in specific situations
A good example of this is when you want to add an effect to a track
but also blend it with the original
So for example I'm going to add a new bus track to this just by going up to my multi track menu
selecting track
add stereo bus track
And it's all a little bit big here
So I'll go over to my header and just scroll my mouse wheel to shrink these two down so I can see them at the same time
And I'll go in and rename my bus a I'll rename this
let's call it Reverb bus
And as the name suggests
I want to add some reverb to this
So I'll go over to my effects rack
I'll go to my first effect option here and down to reverb
let's select Studio Reverb
and I think the great hall preset is good
but what I want to do is control this output level
I want to turn the dry all the way down
This is the original signal
how much of the original signal has been mixed into this effect
I don't want any in there
and for the wet I'll turn this all the way up
so really when I apply this to the original signal
I should be hearing nothing but reverb
So let's close that
Now in the previous video
if we wanted to route this track here to the Reverb bus
I would just go over to my output settings and I'd click this drop down and I'd choose my reverb bus here and we should be able to hear the results of that effect now if I play back our timeline
So that's a lot of reverb
What I actually want to do is control my original signal and the effect separately
And for this I'm going to go back up to my output settings and I'm going to send this original track to the master
So this is going straight to my master track now
and then I'll go up to my options up the top here
At the moment
we're on our inputs and outputs
which is what we can see here
But instead I'm going to click this button here for sends
And now we're looking at our send options for the track
This is send number one here
but believe it or not
if I click this scroll bar down here
you can see we've actually got up to 16 sends for each track
And that would be an extremely complex mix if I needed to use all 16 of those sens
I'm just going to go back up to send one here and I'm going to assign this to rever bus
And underneath this we have a volume control and this is a volume control for how much of this track here am I sending to my bus down here
And at the moment
it's turned all the way down
So I'm actually not sending anything to my reverb bus
I'm just going to hold down my option key or Alt if you're on a PC
and click this control here
and that'll reset this back to 0
So now I'm sending all of my signal down to my Rever bus
So now I'm routing this track to the master
but I'm also sending it down to my Reverb bus down here
which is also ultimately going to the master
And when we played this back before with our bus
all we heard was the reverb
whereas now we should hear the original signal and the reverb at the same time
There are so many veterans out there
If you took each veteran individually and helped them
there you go
And what's really good about doing things this way
especially with an overpowering effect like reverb
is I can actually control how much of that effect is being blended to my original
I basically have a wet and dry mix just by using my volume control on the bus here

## 061 Measuring with the Loudness Radar_原文

For a long time
loudness was measured using peak amplitude
So for example
if I told you I had a file with a peak amplitude that was -6 decibels
that doesn't really tell me much about the actual loudness at all
It could be only -6 decibels for a split second
or it could be regularly hitting that level throughout
So simply measuring peak amplitude isn't very specific and allows for a lot of different loudness across files
This is why in recent years
a measurement for what's known as perceived loudness has been established
and this is a more accurate representation of loudness in any given file
If you're delivering for broadcasts
this is something you'll most likely need to know because broadcast has very strict loudness standards
But even if you're just delivering for the web
this is a good way to make sure your mix is consistent and an appropriate level
So I have my session here
and I want to measure its overall loudness
So to do this I'm going to go to my master track because of course all these tracks up here are being routed to my master track down here
And then I'll go with to my effects rack
make sure I've got my track effects on
And then in the first effects rack slot here I'm just going to click the flyout menu here
I'll go down to the special options and I want to select the loudness radar meter
Now it's Once you've finished editing and mixing your session
you'll want to export it
And if you go up to your file menu and go down to export
you'll see there are quite a few options for how you can do this
For this video
we'll focus on the multi-track mixed down options for your session
Nowif I had of selected specific clips or a time range
then these options here would be enabled
As it is
I'm happy to just export the entire session as it is
This brings up our Export multitrack Mix down dialog box
and the first two options are probably pretty familiar to you
Here's the name of our file and where we're going to save it
I'm just going to save this to the media folder in my exercise files
Underneath that
we have the format we want to save the file in
And we actually have a list here of all the different formats that we can export as so uncompressed file formats like wave Pcm or AIF
a good for high quality
but large files if this is something you want to share on the web
you'll probably want to use a compressed format
something like an MP 3
an AAC
which will be lower quality
but smaller files
Let's keep this as Wave Pcm
Next up
we have the sample type
which refers to both the sample rate and the bit depth of your file
Most of the time you'll want to keep this as it is
but if you want to change any of these options here
you can just click the change button and you can edit any of the settings here
Then we have the format settings
and these of course
will be dependent on what format you've selected
As you can see
if I click the change button here
I can actually choose a higher bit depth because I have wave form selected
But if I was on a different format
maybe something like MP 3
then these settings will relate to the bitrate of the file
I'll just set that back to the way it was
And then down here we have our mixed down options
and there's actually a bit of flexibility here
So I'll just click on this
So at the top here
we have our master track and I can export this as a mono version
so one channel or a stereo version
so 2 channel or 5．1
which is actually 6 channels
probably best to keep this as the number of channels as your master track
which in this case is stereo
But below that
I can actually export each individual track as well if I wanted to You may recall I originally sent this project over from Premiere
and now that I've done all my work in Audition
I want to send it back
Before I do this
I recommend opening up your Premiere project and having the sequence that you want to send the audition files to already loaded
So I have my project relos sequence open at the moment
Now
if I jump back to audition
all I need to do is go up to my multi track menu and select export to Adobe Premiere Pro
So this file here is the XML file that will be used to sync my audition session with my Premiere sequence
And this is the location that that XML file will be saved
along with all the audio files that I export
I'm going to set this to the Media folder alongside my exercise files
Make sure that the sample rate of your export matches the sample rate of your sequence in Premiere
just to make sure everything's coming in correctly
And then we have this option down here where we can either choose to export each track as a stem
which basically means each of these tracks here will be its own file
This is the option to go with if you intend to continue editing in Premiere
because it'll give you more flexibility with all your audio elements separated into tracks
Otherwisewe can choose to mix down the whole session to either a mono stereo or 5．1 file
I think I'd like to continue editing in Premiere
so I'll export each track as a stem
So then I'll go and click Exports
And if it needs to overwrite any media

## 064 Export to Media Encoder_原文

If you're working on a session with video and you don't need to return to Premiere Pro to make any changes
you can also export directly to Adobe Media Encoder
This will allow you to export your session to any number of video formats
To do this
you just need to have your session loaded and then go up to the file menu down to export
exportexport
With Adobe Media Encoder up the top
we can choose the file name for the file we want to create and the location for where we want to save it to
I've just saved mine to my media folder alongside my exercise files
Next up
we can choose the Media Encoder format
And I'd like to publish this for the web
So I think something like H 264 is probably a good format to choose
And now we can choose a preset for that format
So because I want to publish this to something like YouTube
we do have a YouTube 1080 P preset that we can use
Nowunfortunately
we can only choose a preset
We can't actually change it settings
which is a little restrictive and a big difference from exporting this through Premiere Pro
If you did want different settings other than these presets
you'd need to go to Media Encoder first
create a new preset before you come back into Audition
and then select it here
So it can be a bit frustrating
Below this
we have our routing options
And most of the time you probably won't need to touch this
but if you're delivering something like a split track version of your edit where you have one file but the channels are separated into dialogue
musicand sound effects
this is where you would go to actually do all that routing
And then when you're ready to export to Adobe Media Encoder
just click OK
First
it will prepare the files before it sends them over to Adobe Media Encoder
And then once it's done
it will automatically load the session in Media Encoder and start exporting it straight away
And there it is
it's all done

So I'll just click this link here
It'll take me to where we saved the actual file
and I'll just preview this to check the start of the file and make sure everything sounds okay

there's a little over 37000 not for profit organizations dedicated to military causes

## 065 Exporting a session to OMF and XML_原文

If you need to share your files with other editors or audio engineers
two common formats you can use are OMF and XML
and we can create both of these by selecting File Export
So down here we have OMF or Open Media Framework
and this is a format that's been around for quite a while
I'll just click this to bring up our dialog box and I can set the name of the OMF file and where I want to save it to
We can also change the sample type if we want
but it's probably best to keep this the same as what our session is set to
We also have some OMF settings here
and this is where the important decisions are made
And if someone has requested an OMF from you
it's probably best to find out what they prefer here
For our media
we can choose encapsulated or referenced
So encapsulated will create a single OMF file and all the media will be wrapped up inside of it
kind of like a zipped file referenced will actually save the individual media files in the same folder as the OMF file
It's worth mentioning that OMF files actually have a limit of two gig in size
So for some sessions
you may have to choose referenced or divide your session into multiple encapsulated omfs To overcome this limit
I think I'll choose referenced in this case
and the media format looks fine to me For the media options
we can either just copy across each audio file used in the session in its entirety
or we do have this option here to trim audio file files to the clip lengths
which will only copy across what's being used in the session
And then we have the option to specify handles for those files
So we can add an extra second of audio in the beginning and end of each clip
which will give the person who receives the file more flexibility when they're working with them
Most audio engineers that I've worked with will ask for at least 10 seconds worth of handles
but it's definitely worth asking them first
So I'll click okay on those settings
It's probably worth also pointing out that we have a list of warnings here when converting to OMF
as there are several unsupported features like clip and track effects
So I'm happy with these settings
So I'll click Export
and I'll just overwrite anything that I've already exported
The good thing about Audition is it not only can export the OMF format
it can also read it
So if I wanted to double check that everything has exported
okayI can just go up to my file menu and click open
And I'll go to that folder where we've created all of that media
And there's our OMF file
And I'll just click open on that
And now I can see how everything has been converted to OMF
To close this I'm just going to select the file
In my Files panel
go up to File and say Close Session
and it's media
And I'll just jump back to the original session that we had open at the start
Now for the FCP XML
it's a slightly newer format for sharing audio sessions
and it's actually the format that Audition is using for sharing projects with Premiere
So to export an XML from here
we just go up to our file menu
export XML
We get this warning that the constant power panning mode is not supported in this file format
I'll just click okay on that
And again
we can choose a file name
choose a location
Now we could just save the XML by itself and have it reference all of our original media
But if we're sending this to someone else
it's probably a good idea to get all that media and XML in one folder
So for that
I would recommend checking save copies of associated files
I'll just click the options button there
Now
as with the OMF format
we can copy entire audio files if we want
or we can also copy source files trimmed to clip lengths
And we also have the option to set our handles for that
So let's make sure that's 10 seconds there
We can also check this box up the top here if we wanted to convert the files
And this is handy if you have a session that's using all different types of audio format and you just want to convert it to one format

It's all been converted from a multitrack session into an XML file
And if ​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌I go over to my Files panel here
you can see there's the XML file that it's created
If I wanted to see where this has been saved
I can just select this and right click it and I'll choose reveal in Finder and there's the XML file along with all of the media that was copied for that file
So these are two common ways to share your sessions with other people
and which format you choose will really be dependent on what the other person has requested and the specs they've provided
